# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# OpenJDK JVM Bytecode Interpretation Loop

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in openjdk/jdk that implement the JVM bytecode interpreter main dispatch loop: the bytecode dispatch table, the interpreter template generation, and the method entry point setup.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/jdk--742e735d.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/jdk--742e735d` (openjdk/jdk)

```json
{
  "files": [

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

## Summary

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` and includes:

### **62 C++ Source Files** implementing:

1. **Platform-independent core** (10 files):
   - `templateInterpreter.hpp/cpp` - Defines DispatchTable with `_active_table`, `_normal_table`, `_safept_table`
   - `templateInterpreterGenerator.hpp/cpp` - Generates all bytecode templates and entry points
   - `templateTable.hpp/cpp` - Template class definitions for each bytecode
   - `interpreter.hpp/cpp` - Shared interpreter utilities
   - `abstractInterpreter.hpp/cpp` - Abstract interpreter base

2. **Zero interpreter** (4 files) - Alternative interpretation loop using switch statements

3. **CPU-specific implementations** (48 files) across 7 architectures:
   - **X86/X86-64**: 9 files with dispatch_next(), dispatch_via(), load_dispatch_table()
   - **ARM64 (aarch64)**: 8 files
   - **PowerPC**: 8 files
   - **S390**: 8 files
   - **RISC-V**: 8 files
   - **ARM 32-bit**: 8 files

### **Key Architecture Components:**

- **DispatchTable**: Maps 256 bytecodes × 10 TosStates to entry points
- **Template-based code generation**: Each bytecode has optimized code variants
- **Method entry points**: Different paths for native, synchronized, normal methods
- **Dispatch mechanism**: Load bytecode → index into table → jump to handler code → repeat

The files document the complete flow from JVM initialization through bytecode dispatch on each supported CPU architecture.

CPU-specific code. The core mechanism uses a dispatch table to route bytecode execution.\\n\\n**Architecture Overview:**\\n\\nThe interpreter dispatch mechanism consists of three main components:\\n\\n1. **Dispatch Table System** (src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreter.hpp/cpp):\\n   - Defines the `DispatchTable` class which maintains three tables: `_active_table` (current), `_normal_table` (normal mode), and `_safept_table` (safepoint mode)\\n   - Each table maps 256 bytecode values to entry points across 10 TosState (Top-Of-Stack Cache states)\\n   - The `dispatch_table()` method returns pointers to these dispatch tables\\n   - Static instances `_active_table`, `_normal_table`, and `_safept_table` maintain the actual dispatch entries\\n\\n2. **Template Generation** (src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreterGenerator.cpp):\\n   - `generate_all()` creates code templates for each bytecode instruction\\n   - `set_entry_points_for_all_bytes()` populates the dispatch tables with generated code addresses\\n   - `set_safepoints_for_all_bytes()` creates safe entry points for garbage collection\\n   - Each bytecode has up to 10 entry points (one per TosState) for performance optimization\\n\\n3. **Template Definition** (src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateTable.hpp/cpp):\\n   - `Template` class describes code generation properties for each bytecode\\n   - `TemplateTable` maintains static template definitions for all bytecodes\\n   - Each template has flags (uses_bcp, does_dispatch, calls_vm, is_wide) and generator functions\\n\\n**CPU-Specific Dispatch Implementation:**\\n\\nEach CPU architecture implements dispatch via InterpreterMacroAssembler classes:\\n\\n- **X86** (src/hotspot/cpu/x86/interp_masm_x86.cpp): dispatch_next(), dispatch_via(), dispatch_base() - uses indirect jumps through dispatch table with bytecode as index\\n- **ARM64** (src/hotspot/cpu/aarch64/interp_masm_aarch64.cpp): Similar dispatch mechanism with ARM64-specific addressing\\n- **PowerPC** (src/hotspot/cpu/ppc/interp_masm_ppc_64.cpp): Uses PPC load and count register instructions for dispatch\\n- **S390** (src/hotspot/cpu/s390/interp_masm_s390.cpp): S390-specific dispatch implementation\\n- **RISC-V** (src/hotspot/cpu/riscv/interp_masm_riscv.cpp): RISC-V dispatch with register-indirect jumps\\n- **ARM** (src/hotspot/cpu/arm/interp_masm_arm.cpp): 32-bit ARM dispatch mechanism\\n\\nThe dispatch flow:\\n1. Load next bytecode from code buffer (bcp)\\n2. Use bytecode as index into dispatch table\\n3. Jump to table entry (interpreter code for that bytecode)\\n4. Bytecode handler executes and loads next bytecode\\n5. Dispatch repeats\\n\\n**Method Entry Points:**\\n\\nTemplateInterpreterGenerator variants generate method entry points:\\n- `generate_method_entry()` creates entry code for different method types (native, synchronized, etc.)\\n- `generate_normal_entry()` sets up interpreter frame and initializes entry points\\n- `generate_native_entry()` for native methods\\n- Return entry points via `generate_return_entry_for()` for each TosState\\n\\n**Zero Interpreter Alternative:**\\n\\nFor architectures without JIT compilation:\\n- src/hotspot/share/interpreter/zero/bytecodeInterpreter.cpp implements a switch-based interpreter loop\\n- Direct interpretation without templates\\n- Used on platforms like MIPS, S390 without JIT support\\n\\n**Key Files by Function:**\\n\\n- **Dispatch table initialization**: templateInterpreter.cpp (static instances and copying)\\n- **Entry point setup**: templateInterpreterGenerator.cpp (generic) + per-arch files (CPU-specific generation)\\n- **Bytecode handlers**: templateTable*.cpp files (one per architecture)\\n- **Assembly macros**: interp_masm_*.cpp files for dispatch instructions\\n- **Runtime support**: interpreterRT_*.cpp for calling runtime functions from interpreter\\n- **Frame setup**: abstractInterpreter_*.cpp for frame layout calculations\"\n}\n",

Load next bytecode from code buffer (bcp)\\n2. Use bytecode as index into dispatch table\\n3. Jump to table entry (interpreter code for that bytecode)\\n4. Bytecode handler executes and loads next bytecode\\n5. Dispatch repeats\\n\\n**Method Entry Points:**\\n\\nTemplateInterpreterGenerator variants generate method entry points:\\n- `generate_method_entry()` creates entry code for different method types (native, synchronized, etc.)\\n- `generate_normal_entry()` sets up interpreter frame and initializes entry points\\n- `generate_native_entry()` for native methods\\n- Return entry points via `generate_return_entry_for()` for each TosState\\n\\n**Zero Interpreter Alternative:**\\n\\nFor architectures without JIT compilation:\\n- src/hotspot/share/interpreter/zero/bytecodeInterpreter.cpp implements a switch-based interpreter loop\\n- Direct interpretation without templates\\n- Used on platforms like MIPS, S390 without JIT support\\n\\n**Key Files by Function:**\\n\\n- **Dispatch table initialization**: templateInterpreter.cpp (static instances and copying)\\n- **Entry point setup**: templateInterpreterGenerator.cpp (generic) + per-arch files (CPU-specific generation)\\n- **Bytecode handlers**: templateTable*.cpp files (one per architecture)\\n- **Assembly macros**: interp_masm_*.cpp files for dispatch instructions\\n- **Runtime support**: interpreterRT_*.cpp for calling runtime functions from interpreter\\n- **Frame setup**: abstractInterpreter_*.cpp for frame layout calculations\"\n}\n",
